## Section 001: Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed title names the theme without stating what the entrypoint actually is, a mode-selection contract that turns vague Kotlin backend requests into decision-complete work packets before any code is written
- **supporting_reason:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the skill's first instruction is to choose one or more of nine modes before planning or coding, so an entrypoint description that skips mode selection drops the step everything downstream assumes
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the entrypoint framing does not fit Android UI work, multiplatform client work, or generic Kotlin syntax questions, which the skill's guardrails explicitly exclude
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this reference describes how to enter and drive the kotlin-backend-delivery skill and does not restate the framework doctrine its bundled references carry
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to open by defining the entrypoint as spec-first mode selection, name the nine modes, and state the preservation rule for framework, build tool, and versions
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the skill treats framework choice as a conservation problem, Spring Boot versus Ktor is preserved rather than decided, unless the user explicitly requests a migration
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 02 on recommended default: the defensible default is to classify the backend surface, select modes from the nine-mode menu, and write executable requirements before touching implementation

- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 02 on recommended default: the default assumes the following scope: this reference describes how to enter and drive the kotlin-backend-delivery skill and does not restate the framework doctrine its bundled references carry
- **revision_decision:** Section 001 "Kotlin Backend Skill Entrypoint", Question 02 on recommended default: make the default operational by stating both this action and its handoff: open by defining the entrypoint as spec-first mode selection, name the nine modes, and state the preservation rule for framework, build tool, and versions

### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?

- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: adding all seven reference files as mapped rows would promise coverage this evolution did not perform, since only the entrypoint was read in full
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the table records provenance for this document's claims and does not certify the unread bundled references
- **revision_decision:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to keep the single local row, note that seven bundled references exist as an unread discovery surface, and leave all four external URLs as unretrieved candidates
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 002 "Source Evidence Mapping Table", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the entrypoint is deliberately thin, it holds the mode menu and workflow while pushing doctrine into references, so mapping only SKILL.md is honest but incomplete by design

## Section 007: Anti Pattern Registry Table
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed registry lists three corpus-hygiene failures and omits the anti-patterns the skill legislates against by name, GlobalScope request work, business invariants living only in Bean Validation annotations, JPA entities modeled as ideal data classes, and retries without idempotency
- **supporting_reason:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the SKILL.md writes seven explicit do-not guardrails because these are the failures that ship in real Kotlin services, so the registry should carry them with detection cues
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: importing every guardrail verbatim would duplicate the skill instead of registering the highest-cost patterns with signals
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the registry names entrypoint and delivery failures with detection signals and does not restate the full guardrail list
- **revision_decision:** Section 007 "Anti Pattern Registry Table", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add globalscope-request-work, annotation-only-invariants, naive-jpa-data-class, and retry-without-idempotency rows with review-time detection cues

## Section 009: Agent Usage Decision Guide
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed guide says use this reference when the theme is mentioned, but the real trigger is an act, an agent is about to plan, build, harden, or review a Kotlin JVM backend and must first choose modes
- **supporting_reason:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because mode selection attaches at task intake, and a guide keyed to topic mentions fires too late to shape the work packet
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: keying to every Kotlin mention would open this reference for Android, multiplatform, and syntax questions the guardrails exclude
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the guide routes readers into this reference and does not decide the framework stance, which the workflow owns
- **revision_decision:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to trigger on backend delivery events, new endpoint, auth flow, external client, migration, or review pass, and route each to its default mode combination
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 009 "Agent Usage Decision Guide", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the skill pre-computes routing, its five default combinations map common request shapes to mode sets, so intake classification is a lookup before it is a judgment
### Question 02: What is the recommended default, and why?

## Section 018: Workload Model
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed model bounds one service boundary and twenty-five endpoints per batch but not the entrypoint's own working unit, one work packet per surface with modes fixed once and requirements enumerated before code
- **supporting_reason:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because the costly unit in this theme is an unscoped session, work that spans surfaces without a packet loses the traceability that bounds review effort
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: packet-per-surface budgeting varies with surface size, a message consumer and a full auth flow are both one surface with very different weights
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: the model bounds entrypoint effort per request and does not bound service runtime capacity, which belongs to operations doctrine
- **revision_decision:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to rebound the model around one packet per classified surface, one mode set fixed at intake, and requirement counts as the size signal that triggers splitting
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 018 "Workload Model", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that requirements are the natural splitting currency, when a surface's REQ list outgrows one focused session the skill's own lead-time indicator says the task is two packets

## Section 020: Failure Mode Table

## Section 021: Retry Backpressure Guidance
### Question 01: What decision does this reference help make?
- **current_section_observation:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the seed currently shows that the seed bullets classify verification failures generically and never carry the skill's own retry doctrine, no retries without idempotency, timeout budgets, and failure classification
- **supporting_reason:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision matters because retry advice that skips idempotency converts transient faults into duplicate side effects, which is why the skill's guardrail binds the three conditions together
- **counterargument_or_limit:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: the decision must not conceal this limit: the idempotency precondition is about service-level retries, and applying it to documentation-verification retries would be a category error this section must keep separate
- **assumptions_and_boundaries:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: apply the decision only within this boundary: this governs both retrying entrypoint verification work and the retry guidance the entrypoint gives services, kept as two labeled layers
- **revision_decision:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: revise the section to add the service-layer rule, retries require idempotency, timeout budgets, and failure classification, alongside the existing documentation-layer retry bullets
- **additional_insight_to_add:** Section 021 "Retry Backpressure Guidance", Question 01 on governing decision: add the consequence that the skill's retry guardrail is really a design-order rule, idempotency is a property you build before retrying, not a flag you enable after
